        <b>
         Clockwise from top left
        </b>

        <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Resaca_de_la_Palma" title="Battle of Resaca de la Palma">
         Battle of Resaca de la Palma
        </a>
        , American victory
        <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Churubusco" title="Battle of Churubusco">
         at Churubusco
        </a>
        outside Mexico City, U.S. marines
        <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chapultepec" title="Battle of Chapultepec">
         storming Chapultepec castle
        </a>
        under a large American flag,
        <a href="/wiki/Winfield_Scott" title="Winfield Scott">
         Winfield Scott
        </a>
        entering
        <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%B3calo" title="Zcalo">
         Plaza de la Constitucin
        </a>
        after the
        <a href="/wiki/Battle_for_Mexico_City" title="Battle for Mexico City">
         Fall of Mexico City
        </a>
        .

           <p>

             <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Guadalupe_Hidalgo" title="Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo">
              Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             Mexican recognition of
             <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">
              Texas
             </a>
             (among other territories) as independent; End of
             <a href="/wiki/Texas_Revolution" title="Texas Revolution">
              conflict
             </a>
             between Mexico and Texas.
            </li>
           </ul>

       <td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;">
        <span class="metadata">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Mexico.svg">
          <img alt="Portal icon" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="840" height="9" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_Mexico.svg/16px-Flag_of_Mexico.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_Mexico.svg/24px-Flag_of_Mexico.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_Mexico.svg/32px-Flag_of_Mexico.svg.png 2x" width="16"/>

        <a href="/wiki/Portal:Mexico" title="Portal:Mexico">
         Mexico portal
        </a>

      <tr>
       <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;">
        <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
         <ul>
          <li class="nv-view">
           <a href="/wiki/Template:History_of_Mexico" title="Template:History of Mexico">
            <span title="View this template">
             v
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
          <li class="nv-talk">
           <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:History_of_Mexico" title="Template talk:History of Mexico">
            <span title="Discuss this template">
             t
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
          <li class="nv-edit">
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:History_of_Mexico&amp;action=edit">
            <span title="Edit this template">
             e
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </div>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      The
      <b>
       MexicanAmerican War
      </b>
      , also known as the
      <b>
       Mexican War
      </b>
      , the
      <b>
       U.S.Mexican War
      </b>
      or the
      <b>
       Invasion of Mexico
      </b>
      , was an armed conflict between the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
       United States
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Centralist_Republic_of_Mexico" title="Centralist Republic of Mexico">
       Centralist Republic of Mexico
      </a>
      (which became the
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Federal_Republic_of_Mexico" title="Second Federal Republic of Mexico">
       Second Federal Republic of Mexico
      </a>
      during the war) from 1846 to 1848. It followed in the wake of the 1845 U.S.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Texas_Annexation" title="Texas Annexation">
       annexation of Texas
      </a>
      , which Mexico considered part of its territory, despite the 1836
      <a href="/wiki/Texas_Revolution" title="Texas Revolution">
       Texas Revolution
      </a>
      . It was the fourth of the five major wars fought on American soil which was preceded by the
      <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">
       Seven Years' War
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">
       American Revolutionary War
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">
       War of 1812
      </a>
      and succeeded by the
      <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">
       American Civil War
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Combat operations lasted a year and a half, from the spring of 1846 to the fall of 1847. American forces quickly occupied
      <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_de_Nuevo_M%C3%A9xico" title="Santa Fe de Nuevo Mxico">
       Santa Fe de Nuevo Mxico
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Alta_California_Territory" title="Alta California Territory">
       Alta California Territory
      </a>
      , then invaded parts of
      <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_Mexico" title="Northeastern Mexico">
       Northeastern Mexico
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northwest_Mexico" title="Northwest Mexico">
       Northwest Mexico
      </a>
      ; meanwhile, the
      <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Squadron" title="Pacific Squadron">
       Pacific Squadron
      </a>
      conducted a blockade, and took control of several garrisons on the Pacific coast farther south in
      <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Territory" title="Baja California Territory">
       Baja California Territory
      </a>
      . Another American army captured
      <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">
       Mexico City
      </a>
      , and the war ended in a victory for the United States.
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Guadalupe_Hidalgo" title="Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo">
       Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo
      </a>
      ended and specified the major consequence of the war: the forced
      <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Cession" title="Mexican Cession">
       Mexican Cession
      </a>
      of the territories of
      <a href="/wiki/Alta_California" title="Alta California">
       Alta California
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_de_Nuevo_M%C3%A9xico" title="Santa Fe de Nuevo Mxico">
       Santa Fe de Nuevo Mxico
      </a>
      to the United States in exchange for $15 million. In addition, the United States assumed $3.25 million of debt owed by the Mexican government to U.S. citizens. Mexico accepted the loss of Texas and thereafter cited the
      <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">
       Rio Grande
      </a>
      as its national border.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territorial_expansion_of_the_United_States" title="Territorial expansion of the United States">
       American territorial expansion
      </a>
      to the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_coast_of_the_United_States" title="Pacific coast of the United States">
       Pacific coast
      </a>
      had been the goal of President
      <a href="/wiki/James_K._Polk" title="James K. Polk">
       James K. Polk
      </a>
      , the leader of the
      <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">
       Democratic Party
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The war was, however, highly controversial in the United States, with the
      <a href="/wiki/Whig_Party_(United_States)" title="Whig Party (United States)">
       Whig Party
      </a>
      , anti-imperialists and anti-slavery elements strongly opposed. Heavy American casualties and high monetary cost were also criticized. The political aftermath of the war raised the slavery issue in the United States, leading to intense debates that pointed to
      <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">
       civil war
      </a>
      ; the
      <a href="/wiki/Compromise_of_1850" title="Compromise of 1850">
       Compromise of 1850
      </a>
      provided a brief respite.
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
       Etymology
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      In Mexico, terminology for the war includes
      <i>
       Primera intervencin estadounidense en Mxico
      </i>
      (United States' First Intervention in Mexico),
      <i>
       Invasin estadounidense a Mxico
      </i>
      (United States' Invasion of Mexico), and
      <i>
       Guerra del 47
      </i>
      (The War of 1847).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Background">
       Background
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Background">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Having recently attained
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_independence" title="Mexican independence">
       independence
      </a>
      from
      <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
       Spain
      </a>
      in 1821,
      <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
       Mexico
      </a>
      was fraught with internal struggles that verged on civil war. In 1836 it was relatively united in refusing to recognize the
      <a href="/wiki/Texas_Revolution" title="Texas Revolution">
       independence of Texas
      </a>
      . Mexico threatened war with the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
       United States
      </a>
      if it annexed
      <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Texas" title="Republic of Texas">
       Texas
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Meanwhile, President Polk's spirit of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manifest_Destiny" title="Manifest Destiny">
       Manifest Destiny
      </a>
      was focusing United States interest on westward expansion.
     </p>
     <p>
      The military and diplomatic capabilities of Mexico declined after it attained independence and left the northern half of the country vulnerable to the
      <a href="/wiki/Comanche" title="Comanche">
       Comanche
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Apache" title="Apache">
       Apache
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Navajo_people" title="Navajo people">
       Navajo
      </a>
      Indians. The Indians, especially the Comanche, took advantage of Mexico's weakness to undertake large-scale raids hundreds of miles deep into the country to steal livestock for their own use and to supply an expanding market in Texas and the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Indian raids left thousands of people dead and devastated northern Mexico. When American troops entered northern Mexico in 1846 they found a demoralized people. There was little resistance to the Americans from the civilian population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      (See:
      <a href="/wiki/Comanche%E2%80%93Mexico_Wars" title="ComancheMexico Wars">
       ComancheMexico Wars
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Apache%E2%80%93Mexico_Wars" title="ApacheMexico Wars">
       ApacheMexico Wars
      </a>
      )
     </p>
     <p>
      Hostile native activity also made communications and trade between the interior of Mexico and provinces such as Alta California and
      <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_de_Nuevo_M%C3%A9xico" title="Santa Fe de Nuevo Mxico">
       New Mexico
      </a>
      difficult. As a result, New Mexico was dependent on the overland
      <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_Trail" title="Santa Fe Trail">
       Santa Fe Trail
      </a>
      trade with the United States at the outbreak of the MexicanAmerican War.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Designs_on_California">
       Designs on California
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Designs on California">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      An American diplomatic mission in
      <a href="/wiki/1829" title="1829">
       1829
      </a>
      , led by
      <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Butler_(diplomat)" title="Anthony Butler (diplomat)">
       Anthony Butler
      </a>
      , attempted to bribe the Mexican government to give the port of
      <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">
       San Francisco
      </a>
      to the United States, as well as to cease claiming disputed territory near what was then the U.S.-Mexican border (which is now roughly the boundary between Louisiana and Texas).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1842 the American minister in Mexico,
      <a href="/wiki/Waddy_Thompson,_Jr." title="Waddy Thompson, Jr.">
       Waddy Thompson, Jr.
      </a>
      , suggested Mexico might be willing to cede California to settle debts, saying: "As to Texas, I regard it as of very little value compared with California, the richest, the most beautiful, and the healthiest country in the world... with the acquisition of Upper California we should have the same ascendency on the Pacific... France and England both have had their eyes upon it."
     </p>
     <p>
      President
      <a href="/wiki/John_Tyler" title="John Tyler">
       John Tyler
      </a>
      's administration suggested a tripartite pact that would settle the
      <a href="/wiki/Oregon_boundary_dispute" title="Oregon boundary dispute">
       Oregon boundary dispute
      </a>
      and provide for the cession of the port of San Francisco;
      <a href="/wiki/George_Hamilton-Gordon,_4th_Earl_of_Aberdeen" title="George Hamilton-Gordon, 4th Earl of Aberdeen">
       Lord Aberdeen
      </a>
      declined to participate but said Britain had no objection to U.S. territorial acquisition there.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The British minister in Mexico,
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Pakenham" title="Richard Pakenham">
       Richard Pakenham
      </a>
      , wrote in 1841 to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lord_Palmerston" title="Lord Palmerston">
       Lord Palmerston
      </a>
      urging "to establish an English population in the magnificent Territory of Upper California", saying that "no part of the World offering greater natural advantages for the establishment of an English colony... by all means desirable... that California, once ceasing to belong to Mexico, should not fall into the hands of any power but England... daring and adventurous speculators in the United States have already turned their thoughts in this direction." But by the time the letter reached London, Sir
      <a href="/wiki/Robert_Peel" title="Robert Peel">
       Robert Peel
      </a>
      's Tory government with a
      <a href="/wiki/Little_Englander" title="Little Englander">
       Little England
      </a>
      policy had come to power and rejected the proposal as expensive and a potential source of conflict.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Surprisingly, a significant number of influential
      <a href="/wiki/Californio" title="Californio">
       Californios
      </a>
      were in favor of annexation, either by the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
       United States
      </a>
      or by
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">
       Great Britain
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/P%C3%ADo_Pico" title="Po Pico">
       Po de Jess Pico IV
      </a>
      , the last governor of Alta California, was in favor of British annexation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_of_Texas">
       Republic of Texas
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Republic of Texas">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Texas" title="Republic of Texas">
       Republic of Texas
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Texas_Annexation" title="Texas Annexation">
       Texas Annexation
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Texas_Revolution" title="Texas Revolution">
       Texas Revolution
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wpdms_republic_of_texas.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="410" data-file-width="333" height="271" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Wpdms_republic_of_texas.svg/220px-Wpdms_republic_of_texas.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Wpdms_republic_of_texas.svg/330px-Wpdms_republic_of_texas.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Wpdms_republic_of_texas.svg/440px-Wpdms_republic_of_texas.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wpdms_republic_of_texas.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Texas" title="Republic of Texas">
         Republic of Texas
        </a>
        . The present-day outlines of the U.S. states are superimposed on the boundaries of 18361845.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1820,
      <a href="/wiki/Moses_Austin" title="Moses Austin">
       Moses Austin
      </a>
      , a banker from Missouri, was granted a large tract of land in Texas, but died before he could bring his plan of recruiting American settlers for the land to fruition. His son,
      <a href="/wiki/Stephen_F._Austin" title="Stephen F. Austin">
       Stephen F. Austin
      </a>
      , succeeded and brought over 300 families into Texas, which started the steady trend of migration from the United States into the Texas frontier. Austin's colony was the most successful of several colonies authorized by the Mexican government. The Mexican government intended the anglophone settlers to act as a buffer between the Tejano residents and the marauding
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comanches" title="Comanches">
       Comanches
      </a>
      , but the Anglo colonists tended to settle where there was decent
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Farmland" title="Farmland">
       farmland
      </a>
      and trade connections with American Louisiana, rather than westward where they would have been an effective buffer.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1829, as a result of the large influx of American immigrants, the Anglos outnumbered native Spanish speakers in the Texas territory. The Mexican government decided to reinstate the property tax, increase tariffs on American shipped goods, and prohibit slavery. The settlers and many Mexican businessmen in the region rejected the demands, which led to Mexico closing Texas to additional immigration, which continued into Texas illegally, nonetheless, from the United States.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1834, General
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antonio_L%C3%B3pez_de_Santa_Ana" title="Antonio Lpez de Santa Ana">
       Antonio Lpez de Santa Anna
      </a>
      became the centralist dictator of Mexico, abandoning the federal system. He decided to quash the semi-independence of Texas, having succeeded in doing so in Coahuila (in 1824, Mexico had merged Texas and Coahuila into the massive state of
      <a href="/wiki/Coahuila_y_Tejas" title="Coahuila y Tejas">
       Coahuila y Tejas
      </a>
      ). Finally,
      <a href="/wiki/Stephen_F._Austin" title="Stephen F. Austin">
       Stephen F. Austin
      </a>
      called Texians to arms; they declared independence from Mexico in 1836, and after Santa Anna defeated the Texians at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alamo" title="Alamo">
       Alamo
      </a>
      , he was defeated by the
      <a href="/wiki/Texian_Army" title="Texian Army">
       Texian Army
      </a>
      commanded by General
      <a href="/wiki/Sam_Houston" title="Sam Houston">
       Sam Houston
      </a>
      and captured at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_San_Jacinto" title="Battle of San Jacinto">
       Battle of San Jacinto
      </a>
      and signed a treaty recognizing Texas' independence.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Republic_of_Texas_17-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Republic_of_Texas-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Texas consolidated its status as an independent republic and received official recognition from Britain, France, and the United States, which all advised Mexico not to try to reconquer the new nation. Most Texians wanted to join the United States but annexation of Texas was contentious in the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">
       U.S. Congress
      </a>
      , where Whigs were largely opposed. In 1845 Texas agreed to the offer of annexation by the U.S. Congress. Texas became the 28th state on December 29, 1845.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Republic_of_Texas_17-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Republic_of_Texas-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div style="clear:left;">
     </div>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_of_the_war">
       Origins of the war
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Origins of the war">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      The border of Texas as an independent state was originally never settled. The Republic of Texas claimed land up to the
      <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">
       Rio Grande
      </a>
      based on the
      <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_Velasco" title="Treaties of Velasco">
       Treaties of Velasco
      </a>
      , but Mexico refused to accept these as valid, claiming the border as the
      <a href="/wiki/Nueces_River" title="Nueces River">
       Nueces River
      </a>
      . Reference to the Rio Grande boundary of Texas was omitted from the U.S. Congress' annexation resolution to help secure passage after the annexation treaty failed in the Senate. President Polk claimed the Rio Grande boundary, and this provoked a dispute with Mexico.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rives.2C_vol._2.2C_pp._165.E2.80.93168_18-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Rives.2C_vol._2.2C_pp._165.E2.80.93168-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In July 1845, Polk sent General
      <a href="/wiki/Zachary_Taylor" title="Zachary Taylor">
       Zachary Taylor
      </a>
      to Texas, and by October 3,500 Americans were on the
      <a href="/wiki/Nueces_River" title="Nueces River">
       Nueces River
      </a>
      , ready to take over by force the disputed land. Polk wanted to protect the border and also coveted the continent clear to the Pacific Ocean. At the same time Polk wrote to
      <a href="/wiki/Thomas_O._Larkin" title="Thomas O. Larkin">
       Thomas Larkin
      </a>
      , the American consul in Alta California, disclaiming American ambitions in California but offering to support independence from Mexico or voluntary accession to the U.S., and warning that a British or French takeover would be opposed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rives.2C_vol._2.2C_pp._165.E2.80.93168_18-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Rives.2C_vol._2.2C_pp._165.E2.80.93168-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      To end another
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fifty-Four_Forty_or_Fight" title="Fifty-Four Forty or Fight">
       war scare with Great Britain
      </a>
      over the
      <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Country" title="Oregon Country">
       Oregon Country
      </a>
      , Polk signed the
      <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Treaty" title="Oregon Treaty">
       Oregon Treaty
      </a>
      dividing the territory, angering northern Democrats who felt he was prioritizing Southern expansion over Northern expansion.
     </p>
     <p>
      In the Winter of 184546, the federally commissioned explorer
      <a href="/wiki/John_C._Fr%C3%A9mont" title="John C. Frmont">
       John C. Frmont
      </a>
      and a group of armed men appeared in California. After telling the Mexican governor and Larkin he was merely buying supplies on the way to Oregon, he instead entered the populated area of California and visited
      <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_County,_California" title="Santa Cruz County, California">
       Santa Cruz
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Salinas_Valley" title="Salinas Valley">
       Salinas Valley
      </a>
      , explaining he had been looking for a seaside home for his mother.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Mexican authorities became alarmed and ordered him to leave. Frmont responded by building a fort on
      <a href="/wiki/Fremont_Peak_(California)" title="Fremont Peak (California)">
       Gavilan Peak
      </a>
      and raising the American flag. Larkin sent word that his actions were counterproductive. Frmont left California in March but returned to California and assisted the
      <a href="/wiki/California_Republic#Bear_Flag_Revolt" title="California Republic">
       Bear Flag Revolt
      </a>
      in Sonoma, where many American immigrants stated that they were playing "the Texas game" and declared California's independence from Mexico.
     </p>
     <p>
      On November 10, 1845,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Polk sent
      <a href="/wiki/John_Slidell" title="John Slidell">
       John Slidell
      </a>
      , a secret representative, to Mexico City with an offer of $25 million ($681,442,308 today) for the Rio Grande border in Texas and Mexico's provinces of
      <a href="/wiki/Alta_California" title="Alta California">
       Alta California
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_de_Nuevo_M%C3%A9xico" title="Santa Fe de Nuevo Mxico">
       Santa Fe de Nuevo Mxico
      </a>
      . U.S. expansionists wanted California to thwart British ambitions in the area and to gain a port on the
      <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
       Pacific Ocean
      </a>
      . Polk authorized Slidell to forgive the $3 million ($82 million today) owed to U.S. citizens for damages caused by the
      <a href="/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence" title="Mexican War of Independence">
       Mexican War of Independence
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_21-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and pay another $25 to $30 million ($681 million to $818 million today) in exchange for the two territories.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Mexico was not inclined nor able to negotiate. In 1846 alone, the presidency changed hands four times, the war ministry six times, and the finance ministry sixteen times.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Mexican public opinion and all political factions agreed that selling the territories to the United States would tarnish the national honor.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Mexicans who opposed direct conflict with the United States, including President
      <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Joaqu%C3%ADn_de_Herrera" title="Jos Joaqun de Herrera">
       Jos Joaqun de Herrera
      </a>
      , were viewed as traitors.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brooks6162_25-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Brooks6162-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Military opponents of de Herrera, supported by populist newspapers, considered Slidell's presence in Mexico City an insult. When de Herrera considered receiving Slidell to settle the problem of Texas annexation peacefully, he was accused of treason and deposed. After a more nationalistic government under General
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mariano_Paredes_y_Arrillaga" title="Mariano Paredes y Arrillaga">
       Mariano Paredes y Arrillaga
      </a>
      came to power, it publicly reaffirmed Mexico's claim to Texas;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brooks6162_25-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Brooks6162-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Slidell, convinced that Mexico should be "chastised", returned to the U.S.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Conflict_over_the_Nueces_Strip">
       Conflict over the Nueces Strip
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Conflict over the Nueces Strip">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Nueces_Strip" title="Nueces Strip">
       Nueces Strip
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      President James K. Polk ordered General Taylor and his forces south to the Rio Grande, entering the territory that Mexicans disputed. Mexico laid claim to all the lands as far north as the
      <a href="/wiki/Nueces_River" title="Nueces River">
       Nueces River
      </a>
      about 150mi (240km) north of the
      <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">
       Rio Grande
      </a>
      . The U.S. claimed that the border was the Rio Grande, citing the 1836
      <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_Velasco" title="Treaties of Velasco">
       Treaties of Velasco
      </a>
      . Mexico rejected the treaties and refused to negotiate; it claimed all of Texas.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Taylor ignored Mexican demands to withdraw to the Nueces. He constructed a makeshift fort (later known as
      <a href="/wiki/Fort_Brown" title="Fort Brown">
       Fort Brown/Fort Texas
      </a>
      ) on the banks of the Rio Grande opposite the city of
      <a href="/wiki/Matamoros,_Tamaulipas" title="Matamoros, Tamaulipas">
       Matamoros, Tamaulipas
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Mexican forces under General
      <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Arista" title="Mariano Arista">
       Mariano Arista
      </a>
      prepared for war. On April 25, 1846, a 2,000-strong Mexican cavalry detachment attacked a 70-man U.S. patrol under the command of Captain Seth Thornton, which had been sent into the contested territory north of the Rio Grande and south of the Nueces River. In the
      <a href="/wiki/Thornton_Affair" title="Thornton Affair">
       Thornton Affair
      </a>
      , the Mexican cavalry routed the patrol, killing 16 American soldiers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Declarations_of_war">
       Declarations of war
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Declarations of war">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <table class="navbox" style="border-spacing:0;margin:0;float:right;clear:right;width:315px;margin-bottom:0.5em;margin-left:1em;">
      <tr>
       <td style="padding:2px">
        <table class="nowraplinks collapsible autocollapse navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit">
         <tr>
          <th class="navbox-title" colspan="2" scope="col" style="background-color:#B0C4DE;">
           <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
            <ul>
             <li class="nv-view">
              <a href="/wiki/Template:Campaignbox_Texas_Campaign" title="Template:Campaignbox Texas Campaign">
               <span style=";background-color:#B0C4DE;;background:none transparent;border:none;" title="View this template">
                v
               </span>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li class="nv-talk">
              <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Campaignbox_Texas_Campaign" title="Template talk:Campaignbox Texas Campaign">
               <span style=";background-color:#B0C4DE;;background:none transparent;border:none;" title="Discuss this template">
                t
               </span>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li class="nv-edit">
              <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Campaignbox_Texas_Campaign&amp;action=edit">
               <span style=";background-color:#B0C4DE;;background:none transparent;border:none;" title="Edit this template">
                e
               </span>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
           <div style="font-size:110%">
            <span style="line-height:1.6em">
             <a href="/wiki/Texas_Campaign" title="Texas Campaign">
              Texas Campaign
             </a>
            </span>
           </div>
          </th>
         </tr>
         <tr style="height:2px">
          <td colspan="2">
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" colspan="2" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
           <div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
            <ul>
             <li>
              <a href="/wiki/Thornton_Affair" title="Thornton Affair">
               Thornton Affair
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Fort_Texas" title="Siege of Fort Texas">
               Siege of Fort Texas
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Palo_Alto" title="Battle of Palo Alto">
               Battle of Palo Alto
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Resaca_de_la_Palma" title="Battle of Resaca de la Palma">
               Battle of Resaca de la Palma
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </td>
         </tr>
        </table>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mexican%E2%80%93American_War_(without_Scott%27s_Campaign)-en.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1230" data-file-width="1433" height="386" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War_%28without_Scott%27s_Campaign%29-en.svg/450px-Mexican%E2%80%93American_War_%28without_Scott%27s_Campaign%29-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War_%28without_Scott%27s_Campaign%29-en.svg/675px-Mexican%E2%80%93American_War_%28without_Scott%27s_Campaign%29-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War_%28without_Scott%27s_Campaign%29-en.svg/900px-Mexican%E2%80%93American_War_%28without_Scott%27s_Campaign%29-en.svg.png 2x" width="450"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mexican%E2%80%93American_War_(without_Scott%27s_Campaign)-en.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Overview map of the war.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In early 1846 relations between the two countries had deteriorated considerably and on April 23, 1846 the president of Mexico issued a proclamation, declaring Mexico's intent to fight a "defensive war" against the encroachment of the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tucker_2013_p.718_30-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Tucker_2013_p.718-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On April 25, 1846 2,000 Mexican cavalry crossed into the disputed territory and routed a small detachment of American soldiers sparking the "Thornton Affair"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tucker_2013_p.718_30-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Tucker_2013_p.718-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Polk received word of the Thornton Affair, which, added to the Mexican government's rejection of Slidell, Polk believed, constituted a
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Casus_belli" title="Casus belli">
        casus belli
       </a>
      </i>
      (cause for war).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His message to
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">
       Congress
      </a>
      on May 11, 1846, stated that "Mexico has passed the boundary of the United States, has invaded our territory and shed American blood upon American soil."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Congress approved the declaration of war on May 13, with southern Democrats in strong support. Sixty-seven Whigs voted against the war on a key slavery amendment,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bauer68_34-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Bauer68-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but on the final passage only 14
      <a href="/wiki/Whig_Party_(United_States)" title="Whig Party (United States)">
       Whigs
      </a>
      voted no,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bauer68_34-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Bauer68-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      including Rep.
      <a href="/wiki/John_Quincy_Adams" title="John Quincy Adams">
       John Quincy Adams
      </a>
      . Congress declared war on Mexico on May 13, 1846, after only having a few hours to debate. Although
      <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Paredes" title="Mariano Paredes">
       President Paredes
      </a>
      issued a manifesto on May 23 and a declaration of a defensive war on April 23, both of which considered by some the de facto start of the war, Mexico officially declared war by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congress_of_Mexico" title="Congress of Mexico">
       Congress
      </a>
      on July 7.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Antonio_L.C3.B3pez_de_Santa_Anna">
       Antonio Lpez de Santa Anna
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Antonio Lpez de Santa Anna">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Once the U.S. declared war on Mexico,
      <a href="/wiki/Antonio_L%C3%B3pez_de_Santa_Anna" title="Antonio Lpez de Santa Anna">
       Antonio Lpez de Santa Anna
      </a>
      wrote to Mexico City saying, he no longer had aspirations to the presidency, but would eagerly use his military experience to fight off the foreign invasion of Mexico as he had before. President Valentn Gmez Faras was desperate enough to accept the offer and allowed Santa Anna to return. Meanwhile, Santa Anna had secretly been dealing with representatives of the U.S., pledging that if he were allowed back in Mexico through the U.S. naval blockades, he would work to sell all contested territory to the United States at a reasonable price.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Once back in Mexico at the head of an army, Santa Anna reneged on both agreements. He declared himself president once again and unsuccessfully tried to fight off the U.S. invasion.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Opposition_to_the_war">
       Opposition to the war
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Opposition to the war">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks plainlist" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%;width: auto; font-size: 100%;">

      </caption>

          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Star_of_the_West" title="Star of the West">

          </i>

          <a href="/wiki/Corwin_Amendment" title="Corwin Amendment">
           Corwin Amendment
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Sumter" title="Battle of Fort Sumter">
           Battle of Fort Sumter
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%">
        <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
         <ul>
          <li class="nv-view">
           <a href="/wiki/Template:Events_leading_to_US_Civil_War" title="Template:Events leading to US Civil War">
            <span title="View this template">
             v
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
          <li class="nv-talk">
           <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Events_leading_to_US_Civil_War" title="Template talk:Events leading to US Civil War">
            <span title="Discuss this template">
             t
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
          <li class="nv-edit">
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Events_leading_to_US_Civil_War&amp;action=edit">
            <span title="Edit this template">
             e
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </div>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      In the U.S., increasingly divided by
      <a href="/wiki/Sectionalism" title="Sectionalism">
       sectional
      </a>
      rivalry, the war was a partisan issue and an essential element in the
      <a href="/wiki/Origins_of_the_American_Civil_War" title="Origins of the American Civil War">
       origins of the American Civil War
      </a>
      . Most
      <a href="/wiki/Whig_Party_(United_States)" title="Whig Party (United States)">
       Whigs
      </a>
      in the North and South opposed it;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jay166_36-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jay166-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      most Democrats supported it.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jay165_37-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jay165-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Southern
      <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">
       Democrats
      </a>
      , animated by a popular belief in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manifest_Destiny" title="Manifest Destiny">
       Manifest Destiny
      </a>
      , supported it in hope of adding slave-owning territory to the South and avoiding being outnumbered by the faster-growing North.
      <a href="/wiki/John_L._O%27Sullivan" title="John L. O'Sullivan">
       John L. O'Sullivan
      </a>
      , editor of the
      <i>
       Democratic Review
      </i>
      , coined this phrase in its context, stating that it must be "our manifest destiny to overspread the continent allotted by Providence for the free development of our yearly multiplying millions."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Northern antislavery elements feared the rise of a
      <a href="/wiki/Slave_Power" title="Slave Power">
       Slave Power
      </a>
      ; Whigs generally wanted to strengthen the economy with industrialization, not expand it with more land. Among the most vocal opposing the war in the House of Representatives was
      <a href="/wiki/John_Quincy_Adams" title="John Quincy Adams">
       John Quincy Adams
      </a>
      of Massachusetts. Adams had first voiced concerns about expanding into Mexican territory in 1836 when he opposed Texas annexation. He continued this argument in 1846 for the same reason. War with Mexico would add new slavery territory to the nation. When the vote to go to war with Mexico came to a vote on May 13, Adams spoke a resounding "NO" in the chamber. Only 13 others followed his lead.
     </p>
     <p>
      Democrats wanted more land; northern Democrats were attracted by the possibilities in the far northwest.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joshua_Giddings" title="Joshua Giddings">
       Joshua Giddings
      </a>
      led a group of dissenters in Washington D.C. He called the war with Mexico "an aggressive, unholy, and unjust war", and voted against supplying soldiers and weapons. He said:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       In the murder of Mexicans upon their own soil, or in robbing them of their country, I can take no part either now or hereafter. The guilt of these crimes must rest on others. I will not participate in them.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         39
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      Fellow Whig
      <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">
       Abraham Lincoln
      </a>
      contested the causes for the war and demanded to know exactly where Thornton had been attacked and American blood shed. "Show me the spot", he demanded. Whig leader
      <a href="/wiki/Robert_Toombs" title="Robert Toombs">
       Robert Toombs
      </a>
      of Georgia declared:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       This war is nondescript.... We charge the President with usurping the war-making power... with seizing a country... which had been for centuries, and was then in the possession of the Mexicans.... Let us put a check upon this lust of dominion. We had territory enough, Heaven knew.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         40
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      Northern
      <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_States" title="Abolitionism in the United States">
       abolitionists
      </a>
      attacked the war as an attempt by slave-owners to strengthen the grip of slavery and thus ensure their continued influence in the federal government. Acting on his convictions,
      <a href="/wiki/Henry_David_Thoreau" title="Henry David Thoreau">
       Henry David Thoreau
      </a>
      was jailed for his refusal to pay taxes to support the war, and penned his famous essay
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Civil_Disobedience_(Thoreau)" title="Civil Disobedience (Thoreau)">
        Civil Disobedience
       </a>
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Democratic Congressman
      <a href="/wiki/David_Wilmot" title="David Wilmot">
       David Wilmot
      </a>
      introduced the
      <a href="/wiki/Wilmot_Proviso" title="Wilmot Proviso">
       Wilmot Proviso
      </a>
      , which aimed to prohibit slavery in new territory acquired from Mexico. Wilmot's proposal did not pass Congress, but it spurred further hostility between the factions.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:War_News_from_Mexico.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1966" data-file-width="1779" height="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/45/War_News_from_Mexico.jpg/290px-War_News_from_Mexico.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/45/War_News_from_Mexico.jpg/435px-War_News_from_Mexico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/45/War_News_from_Mexico.jpg/580px-War_News_from_Mexico.jpg 2x" width="290"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:War_News_from_Mexico.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <i>
         War News from Mexico
        </i>
        (1848)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Caton_Woodville" title="Richard Caton Woodville">
       Richard Caton Woodville
      </a>
      's lithograph,
      <i>
       War News From Mexico
      </i>
      satirizes the reactions of various segments of the American population to the war. The lithograph is generally considered unfavorable to the war's apparent pro-slavery motivations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Defense_of_the_war">
       Defense of the war
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Defense of the war">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Besides alleging that the actions of Mexican military forces within the disputed boundary lands north of the Rio Grande constituted an attack on American soil, the war's advocates viewed the territories of New Mexico and California as only nominally Mexican possessions with very tenuous ties to Mexico. They saw the territories as actually unsettled, ungoverned, and unprotected frontier lands, whose non-aboriginal population, where there was any at all, represented a substantialin places even a majorityAmerican component. Moreover, the territories were feared to be under imminent threat of acquisition by America's rival on the continent, the British.
     </p>
     <p>
      President Polk reprised these arguments in his Third Annual Message to Congress on December 7, 1847.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In it he scrupulously detailed his administration's position on the origins of the conflict, the measures the U.S. had taken to avoid hostilities, and the justification for declaring war. He also elaborated upon the many outstanding financial claims by American citizens against Mexico and argued that, in view of the country's insolvency, the cession of some large portion of its northern territories was the only indemnity realistically available as compensation. This helped to rally congressional Democrats to his side, ensuring passage of his war measures and bolstering support for the war in the U.S.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Opening_hostilities">
       Opening hostilities
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Opening hostilities">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Remember_Your_Regiment,_U.S._Army_in_Action_Series,_2d_Dragoons_charge_in_Mexican_War_1846.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1700" data-file-width="2740" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Remember_Your_Regiment%2C_U.S._Army_in_Action_Series%2C_2d_Dragoons_charge_in_Mexican_War_1846.jpg/230px-Remember_Your_Regiment%2C_U.S._Army_in_Action_Series%2C_2d_Dragoons_charge_in_Mexican_War_1846.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Remember_Your_Regiment%2C_U.S._Army_in_Action_Series%2C_2d_Dragoons_charge_in_Mexican_War_1846.jpg/345px-Remember_Your_Regiment%2C_U.S._Army_in_Action_Series%2C_2d_Dragoons_charge_in_Mexican_War_1846.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Remember_Your_Regiment%2C_U.S._Army_in_Action_Series%2C_2d_Dragoons_charge_in_Mexican_War_1846.jpg/460px-Remember_Your_Regiment%2C_U.S._Army_in_Action_Series%2C_2d_Dragoons_charge_in_Mexican_War_1846.jpg 2x" width="230"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Remember_Your_Regiment,_U.S._Army_in_Action_Series,_2d_Dragoons_charge_in_Mexican_War_1846.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Captain
        <a href="/wiki/Charles_A._May" title="Charles A. May">
         Charles A. May
        </a>
        's squadron of the 2d Dragoons slashes through the Mexican Army lines.
        <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Resaca_de_la_Palma" title="Battle of Resaca de la Palma">
         Resaca de la Palma
        </a>
        , Texas, May 9, 1846
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Fort_Texas" title="Siege of Fort Texas">
       Siege of Fort Texas
      </a>
      began on May 3. Mexican artillery at Matamoros opened fire on Fort Texas, which replied with its own guns. The bombardment continued for 160 hours
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brooks122_43-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Brooks122-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and expanded as Mexican forces gradually surrounded the fort. Thirteen U.S. soldiers were injured during the bombardment, and two were killed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brooks122_43-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Brooks122-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Among the dead was Jacob Brown, after whom the fort was later named.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On May 8, Zachary Taylor and 2,400 troops arrived to relieve the fort.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, Arista rushed north and intercepted him with a force of 3,400 at
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Palo_Alto" title="Battle of Palo Alto">
       Palo Alto
      </a>
      . The Americans employed "flying artillery", the American term for
      <a href="/wiki/Horse_artillery" title="Horse artillery">
       horse artillery
      </a>
      , a type of mobile light artillery that was mounted on horse carriages with the entire crew riding horses into battle. It had a devastating effect on the Mexican army. In contrast to the "flying artillery" of the Americans, the Mexican canons at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Palo_Alto" title="Battle of Palo Alto">
       Battle of Palo Alto
      </a>
      fired at such slow velocities that it was possible for American soldiers to dodge artillery rounds.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Mexicans replied with cavalry skirmishes and their own artillery. The U.S. flying artillery somewhat demoralized the Mexican side, and seeking terrain more to their advantage, the Mexicans retreated to the far side of a dry riverbed
      <i>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Resaca_(channel)" title="Resaca (channel)">
        resaca
       </a>
       )
      </i>
      during the night. It provided a natural fortification, but during the retreat, Mexican troops were scattered, making communication difficult.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brooks122_43-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Brooks122-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      During the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Resaca_de_la_Palma" title="Battle of Resaca de la Palma">
       Battle of Resaca de la Palma
      </a>
      the next day, the two sides engaged in fierce
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hand_to_hand_combat" title="Hand to hand combat">
       hand to hand combat
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Cavalry" title="United States Cavalry">
       U.S. Cavalry
      </a>
      managed to capture the Mexican artillery, causing the Mexican side to retreata retreat that turned into a rout.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brooks122_43-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Brooks122-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Fighting on unfamiliar terrain, his troops fleeing in retreat, Arista found it impossible to rally his forces. Mexican casualties were heavy, and the Mexicans were forced to abandon their artillery and baggage. Fort Brown inflicted additional casualties as the withdrawing troops passed by the fort. Many Mexican soldiers drowned trying to swim across the Rio Grande. Both these engagements were fought prior to war being declared.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Conduct_of_the_war">
       Conduct of the war
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Conduct of the war">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War_campaigns" title="MexicanAmerican War campaigns">
       MexicanAmerican War campaigns
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      After the declaration of war on May 13, 1846, U.S. forces invaded Mexican territory on two main fronts. The
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_War" title="United States Department of War">
       U.S. War Department
      </a>
      sent a U.S. Cavalry force under
      <a href="/wiki/Stephen_W._Kearny" title="Stephen W. Kearny">
       Stephen W. Kearny
      </a>
      to invade western Mexico from
      <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Barracks_Military_Post" title="Jefferson Barracks Military Post">
       Jefferson Barracks
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Fort_Leavenworth" title="Fort Leavenworth">
       Fort Leavenworth
      </a>
      , reinforced by a Pacific fleet under
      <a href="/wiki/John_D._Sloat" title="John D. Sloat">
       John D. Sloat
      </a>
      . This was done primarily because of concerns that Britain might also try to seize the area. Two more forces, one under
      <a href="/wiki/John_E._Wool" title="John E. Wool">
       John E. Wool
      </a>
      and the other under Taylor, were ordered to occupy Mexico as far south as the city of
      <a href="/wiki/Monterrey" title="Monterrey">
       Monterrey
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="California_Campaign">
       California Campaign
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: California Campaign">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_California" title="Conquest of California">
       Conquest of California
      </a>
     </div>
