     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Firstbearflag.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="322" data-file-width="510" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Firstbearflag.jpg/250px-Firstbearflag.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Firstbearflag.jpg/375px-Firstbearflag.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Firstbearflag.jpg/500px-Firstbearflag.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Firstbearflag.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A replica of the first "Bear Flag" now at
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidio_of_Sonoma" title="Presidio of Sonoma">
         El Presidio de Sonoma
        </a>
        , or
        <i>
         Sonoma Barracks
        </i>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Although the U.S. declared war against Mexico on May 13, 1846,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      it took almost three months (until early August 1846) for definitive word of Congress' declaration of war to get to California. American consul
      <a href="/wiki/Thomas_O._Larkin" title="Thomas O. Larkin">
       Thomas O. Larkin
      </a>
      , stationed in
      <a href="/wiki/Monterey,_California" title="Monterey, California">
       Monterey
      </a>
      , worked successfully during the events in that vicinity to avoid bloodshed between Americans and the Mexican military garrison commanded by General
      <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Castro" title="Jos Castro">
       Jos Castro
      </a>
      , the senior military officer in California.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Captain
      <a href="/wiki/John_C._Fr%C3%A9mont" title="John C. Frmont">
       John C. Frmont
      </a>
      , leading a U.S. Army topographical expedition to survey the
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Basin" title="Great Basin">
       Great Basin
      </a>
      , entered the Sacramento Valley in December 1845.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Frmont's party was at Upper Klamath Lake, Oregon Territory, when it received word that war between Mexico and the U.S. was imminent;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the party then returned to California.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Mexico had issued a proclamation that unnaturalized foreigners were no longer permitted to have land in California and were subject to expulsion.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      With rumors swirling that General Castro was massing an army against them, American settlers in the Sacramento Valley banded together to meet the threat.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On June 14, 1846, 34 American settlers seized control of the undefended Mexican government outpost of
      <a href="/wiki/Sonoma,_California" title="Sonoma, California">
       Sonoma
      </a>
      to forestall Castro's plans.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      One settler created the Bear Flag and raised it over Sonoma Plaza. Within a week, 70 more volunteers joined the rebels' force,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      which grew to nearly 300 in early July.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This event, led by
      <a href="/wiki/William_B._Ide" title="William B. Ide">
       William B. Ide
      </a>
      , became known as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bear_Flag_Revolt" title="Bear Flag Revolt">
       Bear Flag Revolt
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      On June 25, Frmont's party arrived to assist in an expected military confrontation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">
       San Francisco
      </a>
      , then called Yerba Buena, was occupied by the Bear Flaggers on July 2.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On July 5 Frmont's
      <a href="/wiki/California_Battalion" title="California Battalion">
       California Battalion
      </a>
      was formed by combining his forces with many of the rebels.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Commodore
      <a href="/wiki/John_D._Sloat" title="John D. Sloat">
       John D. Sloat
      </a>
      , commander of the U.S. Navy's Pacific Squadron, near Mazatlan, Mexico, had received orders to seize San Francisco Bay and blockade California ports when he was positive that war had begun.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Sloat set sail for Monterey, reaching it on July 1.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Sloat, upon hearing of the events in Sonoma and Frmont's involvement, erroneously believed Frmont to be acting on orders from Washington and ordered his forces to occupy Monterey on July 7 and raise the U.S. flag.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On July 9, 70 sailors and
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">
       marines
      </a>
      landed at Yerba Buena and raised the American flag. Later that day in Sonoma, the Bear Flag was lowered and the American flag was raised in its place.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On Sloat's orders, Frmont brought 160 volunteers to Monterey, in addition to the California Battalion.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On July 15, Sloat transferred his command of the Pacific Squadron to Commodore
      <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Stockton" title="Robert F. Stockton">
       Robert F. Stockton
      </a>
      , who was more militarily aggressive.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Walker_p._154_65-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Walker_p._154-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He mustered the willing members of the California Battalion into military service with Frmont in command.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Walker_p._154_65-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Walker_p._154-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Stockton ordered Frmont to
      <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">
       San Diego
      </a>
      to prepare to move northward to
      <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">
       Los Angeles
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As Frmont landed, Stockton's 360 men arrived in San Pedro.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      General Castro and Governor
      <a href="/wiki/P%C3%ADo_Pico" title="Po Pico">
       Po Pico
      </a>
      wrote farewells and fled separately to the Mexican state of Sonora.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Stockton's army entered Los Angeles unopposed on August 13, whereupon he sent a report to the Secretary of State that "California is entirely free from Mexican dominion."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Stockton, however, left a tyrannical officer in charge of Los Angeles with a small force.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Californio" title="Californio">
        Californios
       </a>
      </i>
      under the leadership of
      <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Flores" title="Jos Mara Flores">
       Jos Mara Flores
      </a>
      , acting on their own and without federal help from Mexico, in the
      <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Los_Angeles" title="Siege of Los Angeles">
       Siege of Los Angeles
      </a>
      , forced the American garrison to retreat on September 29.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They also forced small U.S. garrisons in San Diego and Santa Barbara to flee.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Captain William Mervine landed 350 sailors and marines at San Pedro on October 7.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They were ambushed and repulsed at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Dominguez_Rancho" title="Battle of Dominguez Rancho">
       Battle of Dominguez Rancho
      </a>
      by Flores' forces in less than an hour.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Four Americans died, with 8 severely injured. Stockton arrived with reinforcements at San Pedro, which increased the American forces there to 800.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He and Mervine then set up a base of operations at San Diego.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Meanwhile, U.S. Colonel
      <a href="/wiki/Stephen_W._Kearny" title="Stephen W. Kearny">
       Stephen W. Kearny
      </a>
      and his force of about 100 men, who had performed a grueling march across
      <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">
       New Mexico
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Sonoran_Desert" title="Sonoran Desert">
       Sonoran Desert
      </a>
      , crossed the
      <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">
       Colorado River
      </a>
      in late November, 1846.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Stockton sent a 35-man patrol from San Diego to meet them.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On December 7, 100
      <a href="/wiki/Lancer" title="Lancer">
       lancers
      </a>
      under General
      <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Pico" title="Andrs Pico">
       Andrs Pico
      </a>
      (brother of the governor), tipped off and lying in wait, fought Kearny's army of about 150 at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_San_Pasqual" title="Battle of San Pasqual">
       Battle of San Pasqual
      </a>
      , where 22 of Kearny's men (one of whom later died of wounds), including three officers, were killed in 30 minutes of fighting.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The wounded Kearny and his bloodied force pushed on until they had to establish a defensive position on "Mule Hill".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, General Pico kept the hill under siege for four days until a 215-man American relief force arrived.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Frmont and the 428-man California Battalion arrived in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Luis_Obispo" title="San Luis Obispo">
       San Luis Obispo
      </a>
      on December 14
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and Santa Barbara on December 27.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On December 28, a 600-man American force under Kearny began a 150-mile march to Los Angeles.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Flores then moved his ill-equipped 500-man force to a 50-foot-high bluff above the
      <a href="/wiki/San_Gabriel_River_(California)" title="San Gabriel River (California)">
       San Gabriel River
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On January 8, 1847, the Stockton-Kearny army defeated the Californio force in the two-hour
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Rio_San_Gabriel" title="Battle of Rio San Gabriel">
       Battle of Rio San Gabriel
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      That same day, Frmont's force arrived at San Fernando.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The next day, January 9, the Stockton-Kearny forces fought and won the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_La_Mesa" title="Battle of La Mesa">
       Battle of La Mesa
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On January 10, the U.S. Army entered Los Angeles to no resistance.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On January 12, Frmont and two of Pico's officers agreed to terms for a surrender.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Walker_p._246_92-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Walker_p._246-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Articles of Capitulation were signed on January 13 by Frmont, Andrs Pico and six others at a
      <a href="/wiki/Ranch" title="Ranch">
       <i>
        rancho
       </i>
      </a>
      at
      <a href="/wiki/Cahuenga_Pass" title="Cahuenga Pass">
       Cahuenga Pass
      </a>
      (modern-day North Hollywood).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Walker_p._246_92-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Walker_p._246-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This became known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Cahuenga" title="Treaty of Cahuenga">
       Treaty of Cahuenga
      </a>
      , which marked the end of armed resistance in California.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Walker_p._246_92-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Walker_p._246-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <table class="navbox" style="border-spacing:0;margin:0;float:right;clear:right;width:315px;margin-bottom:0.5em;margin-left:1em;">

            </a>

            </a>

            </a>

            </a>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Pacific_Coast_campaign">
       Pacific Coast campaign
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Pacific Coast campaign">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast_Campaign" title="Pacific Coast Campaign">
       Pacific Coast Campaign
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_and_mexican_soldiers_1846-1848.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4288" data-file-width="2848" height="331" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/US_and_mexican_soldiers_1846-1848.jpg/220px-US_and_mexican_soldiers_1846-1848.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/US_and_mexican_soldiers_1846-1848.jpg/330px-US_and_mexican_soldiers_1846-1848.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/US_and_mexican_soldiers_1846-1848.jpg/440px-US_and_mexican_soldiers_1846-1848.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_and_mexican_soldiers_1846-1848.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        US (left) and Mexican (right) uniforms of the period.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/USS_Independence_(1814)" title="USS Independence (1814)">
       USS
       <i>
        Independence
       </i>
      </a>
      assisted in the blockade of the Mexican Pacific coast, capturing the Mexican ship
      <i>
       Correo
      </i>
      and a
      <a href="/wiki/Launch_(boat)" title="Launch (boat)">
       launch
      </a>
      on May 16, 1847. She supported the capture of
      <a href="/wiki/Guaymas" title="Guaymas">
       Guaymas
      </a>
      , Sonora, on October 19, 1847, and landed bluejackets and Marines to occupy
      <a href="/wiki/Mazatl%C3%A1n" title="Mazatln">
       Mazatln
      </a>
      , Sinaloa, on November 11, 1847. After upper California was secure, most of the Pacific Squadron proceeded down the California coast, capturing all major cities of the
      <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Territory" title="Baja California Territory">
       Baja California Territory
      </a>
      and capturing or destroying nearly all Mexican vessels in the
      <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_California" title="Gulf of California">
       Gulf of California
      </a>
      . Other ports, not on the peninsula, were taken as well. The objective of the Pacific Coast Campaign was to capture
      <a href="/wiki/Mazatl%C3%A1n" title="Mazatln">
       Mazatln
      </a>
      , a major supply base for Mexican forces. Numerous Mexican ships were also captured by this squadron, with the USS
      <i>
       Cyane
      </i>
      given credit for 18 ships captured and numerous destroyed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Entering the Gulf of California,
      <i>
       Independence
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       Congress
      </i>
      , and
      <i>
       Cyane
      </i>
      seized
      <a href="/wiki/La_Paz,_Baja_California_Sur" title="La Paz, Baja California Sur">
       La Paz
      </a>
      , then captured and burned the small Mexican fleet at
      <a href="/wiki/Guaymas" title="Guaymas">
       Guaymas
      </a>
      . Within a month, they cleared the Gulf of hostile ships, destroying or capturing 30 vessels. Later, their sailors and marines captured the port of Mazatln on November 11, 1847. A Mexican campaign under
      <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Pineda_Munoz" title="Manuel Pineda Munoz">
       Manuel Pineda
      </a>
      to retake the various captured ports resulted in several small clashes (
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mulege" title="Battle of Mulege">
       Battle of Mulege
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_La_Paz" title="Battle of La Paz">
       Battle of La Paz
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_San_Jos%C3%A9_del_Cabo" title="Battle of San Jos del Cabo">
       Battle of San Jos del Cabo
      </a>
      ) and two sieges (
      <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_La_Paz" title="Siege of La Paz">
       Siege of La Paz
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_San_Jos%C3%A9_del_Cabo" title="Siege of San Jos del Cabo">
       Siege of San Jos del Cabo
      </a>
      ) in which the Pacific Squadron ships provided artillery support. U.S. garrisons remained in control of the ports.
     </p>
     <p>
      Following reinforcement, Lt. Col.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry_S._Burton" title="Henry S. Burton">
       Henry S. Burton
      </a>
      marched out. His forces rescued captured Americans, captured Pineda, and, on March 31, defeated and dispersed remaining Mexican forces at the
      <a href="/wiki/Skirmish_of_Todos_Santos" title="Skirmish of Todos Santos">
       Skirmish of Todos Santos
      </a>
      , unaware that the Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo had been signed in February 1848 and a truce agreed to on March 6. When the American garrisons were evacuated to Monterey following the treaty ratification, many Mexicans went with them: those who had supported the American cause and had thought Lower California would also be annexed like Upper California.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Northeastern_Mexico">
       Northeastern Mexico
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Northeastern Mexico">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The defeats at Palo Alto and Resaca de la Palma caused political turmoil in Mexico, turmoil which
      <a href="/wiki/Antonio_L%C3%B3pez_de_Santa_Anna" title="Antonio Lpez de Santa Anna">
       Antonio Lpez de Santa Anna
      </a>
      used to revive his political career and return from self-imposed exile in Cuba in mid-August 1846.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was Polk's plan to bring back the exiled dictator who had defeated the Texans at the Alamo and Goliad. On 4 August 1846, "Polk negotiated a deal to not only bring Santa Ana back, but to pay him $2 millionostensibly a bribe as an advance payment on the cession of California."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Santa Ana promised the U.S. that if allowed to pass through the blockade, he would negotiate a peaceful conclusion to the war and sell the New Mexico and Alta California territories to the U.S.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Once Santa Anna arrived in Mexico City, however, he reneged and offered his services to the Mexican government. Then, after being appointed commanding general, he reneged again and seized the presidency.
     </p>
     <p>
      Led by Taylor, 2,300 U.S. troops crossed the Rio Grande after some initial difficulties in obtaining river transport. His soldiers occupied the city of
      <a href="/wiki/Matamoros,_Tamaulipas" title="Matamoros, Tamaulipas">
       Matamoros
      </a>
      , then
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Camargo,_Tamaulipas" title="Camargo, Tamaulipas">
       Camargo
      </a>
      (where the soldiery suffered the first of many problems with disease) and then proceeded south and besieged the city of
      <a href="/wiki/Monterrey" title="Monterrey">
       Monterrey
      </a>
      . The hard-fought
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Monterrey" title="Battle of Monterrey">
       Battle of Monterrey
      </a>
      resulted in serious losses on both sides. The American light artillery was ineffective against the stone fortifications of the city. The Mexican forces were under General
      <a href="/wiki/Pedro_de_Ampudia" title="Pedro de Ampudia">
       Pedro de Ampudia
      </a>
      and repulsed Taylor's best infantry division at Fort Teneria.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Urban_Warfare_97-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Urban_Warfare-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nebel_Mexican_War_02_Capture_of_Monterrey.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3769" data-file-width="5131" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Nebel_Mexican_War_02_Capture_of_Monterrey.jpg/250px-Nebel_Mexican_War_02_Capture_of_Monterrey.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Nebel_Mexican_War_02_Capture_of_Monterrey.jpg/375px-Nebel_Mexican_War_02_Capture_of_Monterrey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Nebel_Mexican_War_02_Capture_of_Monterrey.jpg/500px-Nebel_Mexican_War_02_Capture_of_Monterrey.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nebel_Mexican_War_02_Capture_of_Monterrey.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Monterrey" title="Battle of Monterrey">
         Battle of Monterrey
        </a>
        , after a drawing by
        <a href="/wiki/Carl_Nebel" title="Carl Nebel">
         Carl Nebel
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      American soldiers, including many West Pointers, had never engaged in urban warfare before and they marched straight down the open streets, where they were annihilated by Mexican defenders well-hidden in Monterrey's thick adobe homes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Urban_Warfare_97-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Urban_Warfare-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Two days later, they changed their urban warfare tactics. Texan soldiers had fought in a Mexican city before (the
      <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_B%C3%A9xar" title="Siege of Bxar">
       Siege of Bxar
      </a>
      in December 1835) and advised Taylor's generals that the Americans needed to "
      <a href="/wiki/Mouse-holing" title="Mouse-holing">
       mouse hole
      </a>
      " through the city's homes. In other words, they needed to punch holes in the side or roofs of the homes and fight hand to hand inside the structures. Mexican natives called the Texas soldiers the Diablicos Tejanos (the Devil Texans).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This method proved successful.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Eventually, these actions drove and trapped Ampudia's men into the city's central plaza, where howitzer shelling forced Ampudia to negotiate. Taylor agreed to allow the Mexican Army to evacuate and to an eight-week armistice in return for the surrender of the city. Under pressure from Washington, Taylor broke the armistice and occupied the city of Saltillo, southwest of Monterrey. Santa Anna blamed the loss of Monterrey and Saltillo on Ampudia and demoted him to command a small artillery battalion.
     </p>
     <p>
      On February 22, 1847, Santa Anna personally marched north to fight Taylor with 20,000 men. Taylor, with 4,600 men, had entrenched at a mountain pass called
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Buena_Vista,_Coahuila,_Mexico&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Buena Vista, Coahuila, Mexico (page does not exist)">
       Buena Vista
      </a>
      . Santa Anna suffered desertions on the way north and arrived with 15,000 men in a tired state. He demanded and was refused surrender of the U.S. Army; he attacked the next morning. Santa Anna flanked the U.S. positions by sending his cavalry and some of his infantry up the steep terrain that made up one side of the pass, while a division of infantry attacked frontally along the road leading to Buena Vista. Furious fighting ensued, during which the U.S troops were nearly routed, but managed to cling to their entrenched position. The Mexicans had inflicted considerable losses but Santa Anna had gotten word of upheaval in Mexico City, so he withdrew that night, leaving Taylor in control of part of Northern Mexico.
     </p>
     <p>
      Polk mistrusted Taylor, whom he felt had shown incompetence in the Battle of Monterrey by agreeing to the armistice, and may have considered him a political rival for the White House. Taylor later used the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Buena_Vista" title="Battle of Buena Vista">
       Battle of Buena Vista
      </a>
      as the centerpiece of his successful 1848 presidential campaign.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Northwestern_Mexico">
       Northwestern Mexico
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Northwestern Mexico">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On May 14, 1846, President
      <a href="/wiki/James_K._Polk" title="James K. Polk">
       James K. Polk
      </a>
      ordered
      <a href="/wiki/Colonel" title="Colonel">
       Colonel
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Stephen_W._Kearny" title="Stephen W. Kearny">
       Stephen W. Kearny
      </a>
      to set off from
      <a href="/wiki/Fort_Leavenworth" title="Fort Leavenworth">
       Fort Leavenworth
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">
       Kansas
      </a>
      down the Santa Fe trail in order to seize the province of New Mexico.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On August 18, 1846, Colonel Kearny and his troops took Santa Fe after it was abandoned by its Mexican Garrison.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Civilian resistance in
      <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">
       New Mexico
      </a>
      ended in October,
      <a href="/wiki/1846" title="1846">
       1846
      </a>
      , with
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_Treaty_of_Bear_Springs&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The Treaty of Bear Springs (page does not exist)">
       The Treaty of Bear Springs
      </a>
      . The treaty ended a large scale insurrection by the
      <a href="/wiki/Ute_people" title="Ute people">
       Ute
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Zuni_people" title="Zuni people">
       Zuni
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moquis" title="Moquis">
       Moquis
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Navajo_people" title="Navajo people">
       Navajo
      </a>
      tribes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        102
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After the successful conquest of New Mexico,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexander_Doniphan" title="Alexander Doniphan">
       Alexander Doniphan
      </a>
      and other officers with a background in law drew up a temporary legal system for the territory called
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kearny%27s_Code&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kearny's Code (page does not exist)">
       Kearny's Code
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On March 1, 1847,
      <a href="/wiki/Alexander_William_Doniphan" title="Alexander William Doniphan">
       Alexander W. Doniphan
      </a>
      occupied
      <a href="/wiki/Chihuahua_City" title="Chihuahua City">
       Chihuahua City
      </a>
      . He found the inhabitants much less willing to accept the American conquest than the New Mexicans. British consul John Potts did not want to let Doniphan search Governor Trias's mansion, and unsuccessfully asserted it was under British protection. American merchants in Chihuahua wanted the American force to stay in order to protect their business.
      <a href="/wiki/William_Gilpin_(governor)" title="William Gilpin (governor)">
       Major William Gilpin
      </a>
      advocated a march on Mexico City and convinced a majority of officers, but Doniphan subverted this plan. Then in late April, Taylor ordered the First Missouri Mounted Volunteers to leave Chihuahua and join him at Saltillo. The American merchants either followed or returned to Santa Fe. Along the way, the townspeople of
      <a href="/wiki/Parras" title="Parras">
       Parras
      </a>
      enlisted Doniphan's aid against an Indian raiding party that had taken children, horses, mules, and money.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
       <a href="#cite_note-104">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        104
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The civilian population of northern Mexico offered little resistance to the American invasion, possibly because the country had already been devastated by
      <a href="/wiki/Comanche" title="Comanche">
       Comanche
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Apache" title="Apache">
       Apache
      </a>
      Indian raids.
      <a href="/wiki/Josiah_Gregg" title="Josiah Gregg">
       Josiah Gregg
      </a>
      , who was with the American army in northern Mexico, said that "the whole country from New Mexico to the borders of Durango is almost entirely depopulated. The haciendas and ranchos have been mostly abandoned, and the people chiefly confined to the towns and cities."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
       <a href="#cite_note-105">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        105
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Tabasco">
       Tabasco
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Tabasco">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="First_Battle_of_Tabasco">
       First Battle of Tabasco
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: First Battle of Tabasco">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_Tabasco" title="First Battle of Tabasco">
       First Battle of Tabasco
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Commodore
      <a href="/wiki/Matthew_C._Perry" title="Matthew C. Perry">
       Matthew C. Perry
      </a>
      led a detachment of seven vessels along the southern coast of
      <a href="/wiki/Tabasco" title="Tabasco">
       Tabasco
      </a>
      state. Perry arrived at the Tabasco River (now known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Grijalva_River" title="Grijalva River">
       Grijalva River
      </a>
      ) on October 22, 1846, and seized the town Port of
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Frontera,_Tabasco&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Frontera, Tabasco (page does not exist)">
       Frontera
      </a>
      along with two of their ships. Leaving a small garrison, he advanced with his troops towards the town of San Juan Bautista (
      <a href="/wiki/Villahermosa" title="Villahermosa">
       Villahermosa
      </a>
      today). Perry arrived in the city of San Juan Bautista on October 25, seizing five Mexican vessels. Colonel Juan Bautista Traconis,
      <a href="/wiki/Tabasco" title="Tabasco">
       Tabasco
      </a>
      Departmental commander at that time, set up barricades inside the buildings. Perry realized that the bombing of the city would be the only option to drive out the Mexican Army, and avoiding damage to the merchants of the city, withdrew its forces preparing them for the next day.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Intervenci%C3%B3n_estadounidense_en_Tabasco.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1885" data-file-width="2588" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Intervenci%C3%B3n_estadounidense_en_Tabasco.jpg/250px-Intervenci%C3%B3n_estadounidense_en_Tabasco.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Intervenci%C3%B3n_estadounidense_en_Tabasco.jpg/375px-Intervenci%C3%B3n_estadounidense_en_Tabasco.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Intervenci%C3%B3n_estadounidense_en_Tabasco.jpg/500px-Intervenci%C3%B3n_estadounidense_en_Tabasco.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Intervenci%C3%B3n_estadounidense_en_Tabasco.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Tabasco" title="Second Battle of Tabasco">
         Second Battle of Tabasco
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      On the morning of October 26, as Perry's fleet prepared to start the attack on the city, the Mexican forces began firing at the American fleet. The U.S. bombing began to yield the square, so that the fire continued until evening. Before taking the square, Perry decided to leave and return to the port of
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Frontera,_Tabasco&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Frontera, Tabasco (page does not exist)">
       Frontera
      </a>
      , where he established a naval blockade to prevent supplies of food and military supplies from reaching the state capital.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Second_Battle_of_Tabasco">
       Second Battle of Tabasco
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Second Battle of Tabasco">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Tabasco" title="Second Battle of Tabasco">
       Second Battle of Tabasco
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      On June 13, 1847, Commodore Perry assembled the
      <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_Fleet" title="Mosquito Fleet">
       Mosquito Fleet
      </a>
      and began moving towards the
      <a href="/wiki/Grijalva_River" title="Grijalva River">
       Grijalva River
      </a>
      , towing 47 boats that carried a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landing_force" title="Landing force">
       landing force
      </a>
      of 1,173. On June 15, 12 miles (19km) below San Juan Bautista, the fleet ran through an ambush with little difficulty. Again at an "S" curve in the river known as the "Devil's Bend", Perry encountered Mexican fire from a river fortification known as the Colmena redoubt, but the fleet's heavy naval guns quickly dispersed the Mexican force.
     </p>
     <p>
      On June 16, Perry arrived at
      <a href="/wiki/Villahermosa" title="Villahermosa">
       San Juan Bautista
      </a>
      and commenced bombing the city. The attack included two ships that sailed past the fort and began shelling it from the rear.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/David_D._Porter" title="David D. Porter">
       David D. Porter
      </a>
      led 60 sailors ashore and seized the fort, raising the U.S. flag over the works. Perry and the landing force arrived and took control of the city around 14:00.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._press_and_popular_war_enthusiasm">
       U.S. press and popular war enthusiasm
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: U.S. press and popular war enthusiasm">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      During the war, inventions such as the telegraph created new means of communication that updated people with the latest news from the reporters, who were usually on the scene. With more than a decade's experience reporting urban crime, the "penny press" realized the public's voracious need for astounding war news. Moreover, Shelley Streetby demonstrates that the print revolution (1830s-1840s), which preceded the US-Mexican War, made it possible for the distribution of cheap newspapers throughout the country.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        106
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This was the first time in American history that accounts by journalists, instead of opinions of politicians, had great influence in shaping people's opinions about and attitudes toward a war.
     </p>
     <p>
      By getting constant reports from the battlefield, Americans became emotionally united as a community. News about the war always caused extraordinary popular excitement. In the Spring of 1846, news about
      <a href="/wiki/Zachary_Taylor" title="Zachary Taylor">
       Zachary Taylor
      </a>
      's victory at Palo Alto brought up a large crowd that met in a cotton textile town of Lowell, Massachusetts. New York celebrated the twin victories at Veracruz and Buena Vista in May 1847. Among fireworks and illuminations, they had a "grand procession" of about 400,000 people. Generals Taylor and Scott became heroes for their people and later became presidential candidates.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Desertion">
       Desertion
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Desertion">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Churubusco2.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2414" data-file-width="3354" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Battle_of_Churubusco2.jpg/250px-Battle_of_Churubusco2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Battle_of_Churubusco2.jpg/375px-Battle_of_Churubusco2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Battle_of_Churubusco2.jpg/500px-Battle_of_Churubusco2.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Churubusco2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Churubusco" title="Battle of Churubusco">
          Battle of Churubusco
         </a>
        </i>
        by J. Cameron, published by
        <a href="/wiki/Nathaniel_Currier" title="Nathaniel Currier">
         Nathaniel Currier
        </a>
        . Hand tinted lithograph, 1847. Digitally restored.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Desertion was a major problem for the Mexican army, depleting forces on the eve of battle. Most soldiers were peasants who had a loyalty to their village and family, but not to the generals who had conscripted them. Often hungry and ill, under-equipped, only partially trained, and never well paid, the soldiers were held in contempt by their officers and had little reason to fight the Americans. Looking for their opportunity, many slipped away from camp to find their way back to their home village.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The desertion rate in the U.S. Army was 8.3% (9,200 out of 111,000), compared to 12.7% during the War of 1812 and usual peacetime rates of about 14.8% per year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
       <a href="#cite_note-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many men deserted to join another U.S. unit and get a second enlistment bonus. Some deserted because of the miserable conditions in camp. It has been suggested that others used the army to get free transportation to California, where they deserted to join the gold rush;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-foos_109-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-foos-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      this, however, is unlikely as gold was only discovered in California on
      <a href="/wiki/California_Gold_Rush#History" title="California Gold Rush">
       January 24, 1848
      </a>
      , less than two weeks before the war concluded. By the time word reached the eastern U.S. that gold had been discovered, word also reached it that the war was over.
     </p>
     <p>
      Several hundred U.S. deserters went over to the Mexican side. Nearly all were recent immigrants from Europe with weak ties to the U.S.; the most famous group was the
      <a href="/wiki/Saint_Patrick%27s_Battalion" title="Saint Patrick's Battalion">
       Saint Patrick's Battalion
      </a>
      , about half of whom were Catholics from Ireland. The Mexicans issued broadsides and leaflets enticing U.S. soldiers with promises of money, land bounties, and officers' commissions. Mexican guerrillas shadowed the U.S. Army and captured men who took unauthorized leave or fell out of the ranks. The guerrillas coerced these men to join the Mexican ranks. The generous promises proved illusory for most deserters, who risked being executed if captured by U.S. forces. About 50 of the
      <i>
       San Patricios
      </i>
      were tried and hanged following their capture at Churubusco in August 1847.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-foos_109-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-foos-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Scott.27s_Mexico_City_campaign">
       Scott's Mexico City campaign
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Scott's Mexico City campaign">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <table class="navbox" style="border-spacing:0;margin:0;float:right;clear:right;width:315px;margin-bottom:0.5em;margin-left:1em;">
      <tr>
       <td style="padding:2px">
        <table class="nowraplinks collapsible autocollapse navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit">

             <li class="nv-view">

               </span>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li class="nv-talk">
              <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Template_talk:Mexico_City_Campaign" title="Template talk:Mexico City Campaign">

               </span>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li class="nv-edit">

         </tr>
